<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>The <b>Financial Times Stock Exchange 100 Index</b>, also called the <b>FTSE 100 Index</b>, <b>FTSE 100</b>, <b>FTSE</b>, or, informally, the <b>"Footsie"</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ʊ/ short 'oo' in 'foot'">ʊ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>, is a <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_index" title="Stock market index">share index</a> of the 100 <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">companies</a> listed on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> with the highest <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>. It is seen as a gauge of prosperity for businesses regulated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_company_law" title="UK company law">UK company law</a>. The index is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_Group" title="FTSE Group">FTSE Group</a>, a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange_Group" title="London Stock Exchange Group">London Stock Exchange Group</a>.</p>
<p>The index began on 3 January 1984 at the base level of 1000. The highest intra-day value (7,354) was reached on 16 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The highest closing value (7,337) was reached on 13 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wpj_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-wpj-3">[3]</a></sup> The previous peaks having been over 17 years previously, on the last trading day of 1999, during the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bubble</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and in April 2015, when the Index reached 7103.98.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> After falling during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007-2010" title="Financial crisis of 2007-2010">financial crisis of 2007-2010</a> to below 3500 in March 2009, the index recovered to a peak of 6091.33 on 8 February 2011, <a href="/wiki/August_2011_stock_markets_fall" title="August 2011 stock markets fall">then fell again</a> to under the 5000 mark on the morning of 23 September 2011, but reached its record high on the morning of 16 January 2017.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FTSE_100_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The index is maintained by the FTSE Group, a now wholly owned subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> which originated as a joint venture between the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> and the London Stock Exchange. It is calculated in <a href="/wiki/Real-time_computing" title="Real-time computing">real time</a> and published every second when the market is open.</p>
<p>The FTSE 100 consists of the largest 100 qualifying UK companies by full market value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> A large slice of these are international companies, however, so the index's movements are a fairly weak indicator of how the UK economy is faring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> A better indication of the UK economy is the FTSE 250 as it contains a smaller proportion of international companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The constituents of the FTSE are determined quarterly, on the Wednesday after the first Friday of the month in March, June, September and December. The values used to make the changes to the indices are taken at the close of business the night before the review.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>FTSE 100 companies represent about 81% of the entire market capitalisation of the London Stock Exchange. Even though the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_All-Share_Index" title="FTSE All-Share Index">FTSE All-Share Index</a> is more comprehensive, the FTSE 100 is by far the most widely used UK stock market indicator. Other related indices are the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_250_Index" title="FTSE 250 Index">FTSE 250 Index</a> (which includes the next largest 250 companies after the FTSE 100), the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_350_Index" title="FTSE 350 Index">FTSE 350 Index</a> (which is the aggregation of the FTSE 100 and 250), <a href="/wiki/FTSE_SmallCap_Index" title="FTSE SmallCap Index">FTSE SmallCap Index</a> and <a href="/wiki/FTSE_Fledgling_Index" title="FTSE Fledgling Index">FTSE Fledgling Index</a>. The FTSE All-Share aggregates the FTSE 100, FTSE 250 and FTSE SmallCap.</p>
<p>Component companies must meet a number of requirements set out by the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_Group" title="FTSE Group">FTSE Group</a>, including having a full listing on the London Stock Exchange with a Sterling or Euro denominated price on the Stock Exchange Electronic Trading Service, and meeting certain tests on nationality, <a href="/wiki/Public_float" title="Public float">free float</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Market_liquidity" title="Market liquidity">liquidity</a>.</p>
<p>The constituent companies were criticised for their lack of diversity at the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">boardroom</a> level in a 2014 study which found that more than half of them had no non-<a href="/wiki/Caucasian_race" title="Caucasian race">white</a> board members, and two thirds did not have any <a href="/wiki/Executive_director" title="Executive director">executive directors</a> from minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Continuous trading on the London Stock Exchange starts at 08:00 and ends at 16:30 (when the closing auction starts), and closing values are taken at 16:35.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weighting">Weighting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FTSE_100_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Weighting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the FTSE indices, share prices are weighted by market capitalisation, so that the larger companies make more of a difference to the index than smaller companies. The basic formula for these indices is:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>Index level</mtext>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<munder>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</munder>
<msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>Price of stock</mtext>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>Number of shares</mtext>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>Free float adjustment factor</mtext>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
<mtext>Index divisor</mtext>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\text{Index level}}={\frac {\sum _{i}{\text{Price of stock}}_{i}\times {\text{Number of shares}}_{i}\times {\text{Free float adjustment factor}}_{i}}{\text{Index divisor}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\text{Index level}}={\frac {\sum _{i}{\text{Price of stock}}_{i}\times {\text{Number of shares}}_{i}\times {\text{Free float adjustment factor}}_{i}}{\text{Index divisor}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/08e051a215d781d78cdb2e3fb16353826b8ca347" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:86.331ex; height:6.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>The <b>Free float Adjustment factor</b> represents the percentage of all issued shares that are readily available for trading. The factor is then rounded up to the nearest multiple of 5%. To find the free-float capitalisation of a company, first find its market cap (number of shares x share price) then multiply by its free-float factor. Free-float capitalisation, therefore, does not include restricted stocks, such as those held by company insiders.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_constituents_by_market_capitalisation_as_of_February_2016">Current constituents by market capitalisation as of February 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FTSE_100_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Current constituents by market capitalisation as of February 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following table lists the FTSE 100 companies measured by market capitalisation after the most recent changes on 15 February 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The numbers of employees are taken from company reports, mostly dated between 2013 and 2015, and the Financial Times. The index consists of 100 companies, but there are 101 listings, as <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> has both A and B class shares listed. <a href="/wiki/Schroders" title="Schroders">Schroders</a> Non Voting shares were also listed until 1 June 2012 when the FTSE's stricter rules came into force.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_constituents">Current constituents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FTSE_100_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Current constituents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The current constituents following the changes of 19 December 2016 are as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-4" style="-moz-column-count: 4; -webkit-column-count: 4; column-count: 4;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="FT_30">FT 30</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FTSE_100_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: FT 30">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FT_30" title="FT 30">FT 30</a></div>
<p>The oldest continuous index in the UK is the FT 30, also known as the Financial Times Index or the FT Ordinary Index (FTOI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> It was established in 1935 and nowadays is largely obsolete due to its redundancy. It is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>, and companies listed are from the industrial and commercial sectors. Financial sector companies and government stocks are excluded.</p>
<p>Of the original constituents,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> four are currently in the FTSE 100: Guest Keen &amp; Nettlefolds (<a href="/wiki/GKN" title="GKN">GKN</a>), Tate &amp; Lyle, Imperial Tobacco and Rolls-Royce, although Rolls-Royce has not been continuously listed and Imperial Tobacco was a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Hanson_plc" title="Hanson plc">Hanson</a> for a number of years. ICI was removed when it was taken over by Akzo Nobel in January 2008. Two of the original FT 30 companies are still in that index:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> GKN and Tate &amp; Lyle (membership is not strictly based on market capitalisation, so this does not mean they are necessarily among the top thirty companies in the FTSE 100). The best performer from the original lineup has been Imperial Tobacco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
